## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (rate laws / concentration–time ODE models)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is explicitly the time-derivative of a chemical concentration A(t), which is the standard formulation of reaction kinetics as ordinary differential equations. With only (t, A) available, the most likely models are empirical or mechanistic rate laws where the rate depends on concentration (reaction order, autocatalysis, reversible relaxation) and/or explicitly on time (time-varying conditions, forcing).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order rate law: dA_dt = c0 (constant-rate production/consumption under saturation or constant flux)
- First-order decay/production: dA_dt = c0 * A (unimolecular reaction, exponential growth/decay depending on sign of c0)
- n-th order power-law rate: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general mass-action-like order with non-integer order possible empirically)
- Second-order (special case): dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular with one species folded into rate constant)
- General polynomial kinetics: dA_dt = c0 + c1 * A + c2 * A**2 (low-order approximation of complex kinetics near an operating range)
- Linear relaxation to equilibrium: dA_dt = c0 * (A - c1) (approach to steady state A = c1 with timescale set by c0)
- Reversible/competing linear processes: dA_dt = c0 + c1 * A (constant source plus first-order loss; steady state at A = -(c0/c1) when c1<0)
- Autocatalytic / logistic-like kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-accelerating growth with depletion/limitation)
- Inhibited (decelerating) kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (A + c1) (rate increases with A but saturates due to limitation/inhibition)
- Time-dependent rate coefficient (linear drift): dA_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * A (environmental drift/aging causing changing first-order rate)
- Time-dependent rate coefficient (exponential drift): dA_dt = (c0 * exp(c1 * t)) * A (e.g., temperature ramp folded into effective k(t))
- Periodic forcing of kinetics: dA_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * A (diurnal/cycling conditions modulating rate)
- Impulse/activation then decay (gated kinetics): dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(-c1 * (t - c2)**2) (reaction active near a time window, e.g., pulsed illumination)
- Mixed time-and-concentration nonlinearity: dA_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * A**c2 (empirical nonstationary power-law kinetics)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dA_dt is proportional to A (approximately a straight line through the origin when plotting dA_dt vs A), it suggests first-order kinetics with constant rate coefficient.
- If dA_dt scales like A**n (linear in log|dA_dt| vs log A), it suggests an n-th order power-law rate; curvature indicates changing apparent order or additional mechanisms.
- If dA_dt crosses zero at a nonzero A (root at A = A*), it indicates an equilibrium/steady-state concentration; linear dependence on (A - A*) suggests relaxation dynamics.
- If dA_dt is near constant over varying A, it suggests zero-order behavior (rate-limited by catalyst/site saturation, constant feed/withdrawal, or strong excess of another reactant).
- If dA_dt increases with A at low A but plateaus at high A, a saturating rational form like A/(A+c) is indicative of limitation by finite capacity or inhibition.
- If dA_dt vs A is non-monotone (positive at small A, negative at large A, or vice versa), it suggests autocatalysis with depletion/limitation such as A*(c-A).
- If the relationship between dA_dt and A changes over time at fixed A, it implies explicit time dependence in the effective rate coefficient k(t) (e.g., k(t)=c0+c1*t or k(t)=c0*exp(c1*t)).
- If dA_dt shows oscillatory modulation over t at similar A, it suggests periodic forcing in the rate coefficient (sin/cos terms in t).
- If reaction occurs mainly in a time window (rates near zero outside), a localized envelope in t (e.g., Gaussian in (t-c)) can represent pulsed activation or transient availability of a reagent.

GT: -c0*A - c1*A*exp(-c2*_s*t) + c3*_t*sin(log(A + c4))
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []

I need to analyze each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT numerical expression:** `-0.25667*A - 0.25667*A*exp(-0.02054*t) + 0.94264*sin(log(A + 1))`

Let me identify the key basis functions in the GT:
1. A linear term in A: `-0.25667*A`
2. A term `A*exp(-0.02054*t)` (product of A and a decaying exponential in t)
3. `sin(log(A + 1))` - a sine of logarithm composition

This is a very specific functional form. Let me check each candidate for the presence of these basis functions.

**Critical observation:** The GT contains `sin(log(A + 1))`, which is a very unusual basis function. Most candidates don't have `sin(log(...))` - they have either `sin(...)` or `log(...)` separately, but not composed. Also, the GT has `A*exp(c*t)`, which is a product of A and an exponential in t - most candidates don't have this either.

Let me systematically check:

**Term `A*exp(c*t)`:** This requires a term where A multiplies an exponential in t. Looking through candidates, I need `A*exp(...)` type terms. Most candidates have `exp(c*t)` without the A multiplier, or `A/(...)` type terms.

**Term `sin(log(A+c))`:** This is a composition of sin and log. None of the candidates appear to have `sin(log(...))`. They have `sin(c*t + c)` or `log(A*c + 1)` separately.

Let me verify each candidate more carefully:

For all candidates, I need to check:
1. Can they produce `A*exp(c*t)`? - This requires a term that's a product of A and exp(t).
2. Can they produce `sin(log(A+1))`? - This requires sin composed with log.

**None of the candidates have `A*exp(c*t)` as a term** - they have `A*c/(c+t)^n`, `A/sqrt(c+t)`, `A*c`, etc. for A-dependent terms, and `exp(c*t)` without A multiplication.

**None of the candidates have `sin(log(...))`** - they have `sin(c*t+c)` or `log(A*c+1)` but never the composition.

Since the GT requires both `A*exp(c*t)` (a product, not separable into additive terms of A alone and exp(t) alone) and `sin(log(A+1))` (a composition), and no candidate has either of these basis functions, no candidate can match.

Let me double-check a few promising ones:

**Candidate 1:** Has `sin(c3*t + c4)` - this is sin of a linear function of t, not sin(log(A+1)). [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 10:** Has `sin(c5*t + c6)` - same issue. [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 35:** Has `sin(A*c5 + c6)` - sin of a linear function of A, not sin(log(A+1)). [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 34:** Has `sin(c5*t + c6)` and `log(A*c8 + 1)` separately, but not composed. [NO MATCH]

Since `sin(log(A+1))` cannot be decomposed into any sum of elementary functions like `sin(t)`, `log(A)`, `exp(t)`, polynomials, etc., and since `A*exp(c*t)` cannot be written as a sum of functions of A alone plus functions of t alone, none of these candidates can match the GT.
